class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Dominant tree species</th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="mw-redirect" title="Tabonuco">Tabonuco</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Dacryodes_excelsa" title="Dacryodes excelsa">Dacryodes excelsa</a></i>),<br /><i><a href="/wiki/Ausubo" class="mw-redirect" title="Ausubo">Ausubo</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Manilkara_bidentata" title="Manilkara bidentata">Manilkara bidentata</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br /><i><a href="/wiki/Montillo" class="mw-redirect" title="Montillo">Montillo</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sloanea_berteroana" title="Sloanea berteroana">Sloanea berteroana</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Toro Negro State Forest</b> (Spanish: <i>Bosque Estatal de Toro Negro</i>) is one of the 21 forests that make up the public forests system in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is also Puerto Rico\'s highest <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">cloud forest</a>. It is in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Central, Puerto Rico">Cordillera Central</a> region of the island and covers 8,204 cuerdas (7,968 acres; 3,224&#160;ha; 32.24&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), of mountains. Toro Negro\'s mountains have heights reaching up to 4,400 feet (1,300&#160;m) and include <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-places.eyetour.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-places.eyetour.com-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Jayuya" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerro Jayuya">Cerro Jayuya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Rosa" title="Cerro Rosa">Cerro Rosa</a>, the three highest peaks in the island. Nested among these mountains is Lake Guineo, the island\'s highest lake.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_State_Forest._11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_State_Forest.-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest has 18 kilometers (11&#160;mi) of trails, an observation tower, two natural swimming pools (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>:"<i>charcos</i>"), <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">camping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Picnic" title="Picnic">picnic</a> areas, nine rivers, and numerous creeks and waterfalls.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The forest spans areas within the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Orocovis, Puerto Rico">Orocovis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ciales, Puerto Rico">Ciales</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Juana_D%C3%ADaz,_Puerto_Rico" title="Juana D\xc3\xadaz, Puerto Rico">Juana D\xc3\xadaz</a>, and consists of seven non-contiguous tracts of land.<sup id="cite_ref-places.eyetour.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-places.eyetour.com-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro._13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The largest contiguous segment of the forest is located in the municipalities of Ponce and Jayuya.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some 40% of the area of Toro Negro State Forest is located in Ponce\'s <a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">Barrio</a> <a href="/wiki/An%C3%B3n" title="An\xc3\xb3n">An\xc3\xb3n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Historia_de_Nuestros_Barrios_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historia_de_Nuestros_Barrios-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>When created in 1935 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_National_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean National Forest">Caribbean National Forest</a>, the Toro Negro Forest Reserve was managed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States government">United States government</a>, first via the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Reconstruction_Administration" title="Puerto Rico Reconstruction Administration">Puerto Rico Reconstruction Administration</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">Department of the Interior</a> (1935\xe2\x80\x931942) and later through the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Forest_Service" title="United States Forest Service">Forest Service</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">Department of Agriculture</a> (1942\xe2\x80\x931970). Then, in 1970, the Federal Government exchanged with the Government of the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico the Toro Negro section of the Caribbean National Forest for some forested lands belonging to the Commonwealth and located adjacent to the much larger federal lands at <a href="/wiki/Luquillo_National_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Luquillo National Forest">Luquillo National Forest</a> resulting in the creation at Luquillo of the current <a href="/wiki/El_Yunque_National_Forest" title="El Yunque National Forest">El Yunque National Forest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1970, the Government of Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/Departmento_de_Recursos_Naturales_y_Ambientales_de_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Departmento de Recursos Naturales y Ambientales de Puerto Rico">Departmento de Recursos Naturales y Ambientales</a> (DRNA) opened the Toro Negro Forest Reserve as a Commonwealth state forest and renamed it <i>Bosque Estatal de Toro Negro</i> (Toro Negro State Forest).\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_(IMG_3406).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_%28IMG_3406%29.jpg/200px-Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_%28IMG_3406%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_%28IMG_3406%29.jpg/300px-Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_%28IMG_3406%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_%28IMG_3406%29.jpg/400px-Rio_Inabon_along_PR-511_in_Barrio_Real_in_Ponce_%28IMG_3406%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Inab%C3%B3n" title="R\xc3\xado Inab\xc3\xb3n">R\xc3\xado Inab\xc3\xb3n</a> as it makes its way out of the Toro Negro forest</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 1876, Spanish King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_XII_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfonso XII of Spain">Alfonso XII of Spain</a> issued the first proclamation for the creation of forest reserves in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.pwnet.org_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.pwnet.org-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The land where Toro Negro sits was originally used for coffee plantations until the 1930s when a program of reforestation was commenced.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1934, those lands were acquired by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Reconstruction_Administration" title="Puerto Rico Reconstruction Administration">Puerto Rico Reconstruction Administration</a> (PRRA).<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest started with a total of 2,733 hectares (6,750 acres) in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-Indeterminate_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indeterminate-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1935, 1,900 acres (2,000&#160;cda) of private lands were purchased by the PRRA.<sup id="cite_ref-Caribbean_National_Forest._21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caribbean_National_Forest.-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest was not a separate entity at the time; it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_National_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean National Forest">Caribbean National Forest</a>, and was administered by the U.S. Forest Service as the Toro Negro Division of the Caribbean National Forest.<sup id="cite_ref-Caribbean_National_Forest._21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caribbean_National_Forest.-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additional lands brought the total size of the Toro Negro purchase that year to 6,620 acres (6,820&#160;cda),<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and at least an additional 1,385 acres (1,426&#160;cda) were in the process of being acquired in 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Between 1934 and 1945 over 3 million seedlings and approximately 19,000 pounds of seeds were sown on 1,856 acres (1,911&#160;cda) of the forest. Twenty-eight species were planted in twenty-nine different plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1942, the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_the_Interior" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of the Interior">US Department of the Interior</a> transferred the forest to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a>. From 1942 to 1961, it was administered by the <a href="/wiki/US_Forest_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="US Forest Service">US Forest Service</a>. During these years, the U.S. Department of Agriculture continued its acquisition of lands increasing the acreage of Toro Negro.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg/220px-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg/330px-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg/440px-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>Bosque Estatal de Toro Negro</figcaption></figure> \n<p>In 1961, Toro Negro was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">Government of Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The transfer was finalized on 21 May 1962, when the 6,817 cuerdas (6,621 acres) of land that constituted the Toro Negro Unit of the Caribbean National Forest were signed away to the Government of Puerto Rico by the Federal Government. Of these 6,817 cuerdas (6,621 acres), 1,996 cuerdas (1,939 acres) were exchanged for 1,614 cuerdas (1,568 acres) located adjacent to the Luquillo Unit of the Caribbean National Forest. The remaining 4,821 cuerdas (4,682 acres) were ceded to Puerto Rico\'s Department of Agriculture for forestry purposes. This resulted in the Toro Negro State Forest.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Since 1962, approximately 120 <a href="/wiki/Cuerda" title="Cuerda">cuerdas</a> have been planted to <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus_robusta" title="Eucalyptus robusta">eucalyptus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahoe" title="Mahoe">mahoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neolamarckia_cadamba" title="Neolamarckia cadamba">kadam</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Pinus_caribaea" class="mw-redirect" title="Pinus caribaea">Honduran pine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1962, Toro Negro had 6,817 cuerdas (6,621 acres), representing 11.32% of Puerto Rico\'s state forests.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1962 the Area Recreacional Do\xc3\xb1a Juana was added to Toro Negro.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In April 1970, a land exchange which included the Puerto Rico Department of Agriculture purchase and transfer of 1,677 acres (1,727&#160;cda) forest lands adjacent to Luquillo Experimental Forest in exchange for the complete transfer of Toro Negro forest lands to the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The lower elevations of Toro Negro used to be important coffee-producing plantations, however, the entire forest is especially critical for water and soil conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today, the amount of tree foliage coverage in the forest ranges from 81% in the moist forest zone to 99% in the lower montane wet forest zone.<sup id="cite_ref-FINAL_2011_Page_6_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FINAL_2011_Page_6-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest was named for the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Toro_Negro" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Toro Negro">R\xc3\xado Toro Negro</a>, one of nine rivers that flow out of the forest, and the name of one of the <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ciales, Puerto Rico">Ciales</a> portion of the forest.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Protected_area">Protected area</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Protected area"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1237879389"><table class="infobox vcard"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above fn org">Protected Areas at <i>Bosque Estatal de Toro Negro</i></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader" style="font-size: 100%;"><div style="background-color: #B2E5CD;"><a href="/wiki/IUCN_protected_area_categories" title="IUCN protected area categories">IUCN category</a> IV (habitat/species management area)</div></td></tr><tr class="locality"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> (Approx 40%),<sup id="cite_ref-Historia_de_Nuestros_Barrios_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historia_de_Nuestros_Barrios-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br /><a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a> (Approx 30%),<br /><a href="/wiki/Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Orocovis, Puerto Rico">Orocovis</a> (Approx 15%),<br /><a href="/wiki/Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ciales, Puerto Rico">Ciales</a> (Approx 10%),<br />and <a href="/wiki/Juana_Diaz,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Juana Diaz, Puerto Rico">Juana Diaz</a> (Approx 5%)</td></tr><tr class="note"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Nearest&#160;city</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Area</th><td class="infobox-data">7,967.6 acres (3,224.4&#160;ha)</td></tr><tr class="note"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Established</th><td class="infobox-data">1934<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Visitors</th><td class="infobox-data">126,916<sup id="cite_ref-envivopr.com_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-envivopr.com-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>&#32;(in&#160;2008<sup id="cite_ref-envivopr.com_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-envivopr.com-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Governing&#160;body</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico DRNA</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Toro Negro is a <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected area</a> under the law.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The forest has a protected status of "IV" ("Protected Area with sustainable use of natural resources") according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a> (IUCN) convention.<sup id="cite_ref-Indeterminate_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indeterminate-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ecological protection is managed and enforced by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a>.\n</p><p>Through the <i>parcelero</i> (from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> root for "<a href="/wiki/Land_lot" title="Land lot">parcel</a>", or land lot) program, people who were living in the lands being incorporated into the reserve during the federal government land acquisitions of 1935 were allowed to stay in their places when forest protection went into effect.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1999, a bill in the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_House_of_Representatives" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico House of Representatives">Puerto Rico House of Representatives</a> sought to increase the size of the protected area by unifying the Toro Negro, <a href="/wiki/Guilarte_State_Forest" title="Guilarte State Forest">Guilarte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_State_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Pueblo State Forest">Pueblo de Adjuntas</a> State Forests.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In a March 2008 study by its International Institute of Tropical Forestry (IITF), the U.S. Department of Agriculture classified Toro Negro State Forest as a Commonwealth of Puerto Rico forest of "Status 2", s status it defines as "an area having permanent protection from conversion of natural land cover and a mandated management plan in operation to maintain a primarily natural state, but which may receive use or management practices that degrade the quality of existing natural communities".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  As of 2013, there were ongoing governmental initiatives in place to acquire, from private owners, additional lands adjacent to the Toro Negro State Forest to increase the protected area of the forest as well as to create a wildlife forest <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_corridor" title="Wildlife corridor">corridor</a> that would join Toro Negro with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Los_Tres_Picachos_State_Forest" title="Los Tres Picachos State Forest">Tres Picachos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guilarte_State_Forest" title="Guilarte State Forest">Guilarte</a> state forests through plans such as the federal Forest Legacy Areas initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Location">Location</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Toro Negro is located in the central mountainous region of Puerto Rico and it has a total area of 8,203.6977 cuerdas (3,224.3778&#160;ha; 7,967.6110 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is located in remote areas of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> mountain range. The forest office is at km. 32.4 of Route <a href="/wiki/PR-143" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-143">PR-143</a>, east of the intersection with Route <a href="/wiki/PR-149" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-149">PR-149</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest distribution encompasses a range from 18\xc2\xb007\'30" N and 18\xc2\xb015\'00" N to 66\xc2\xb030\'00" W and 66\xc2\xb037\'30" W.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest ranger\'s office and visitors\' area are located on <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_143" title="Puerto Rico Highway 143">Puerto Rico Highway 143</a> Km 32.4 in Barrio Ala de la Piedra, <a href="/wiki/Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Orocovis, Puerto Rico">Orocovis</a> at 18.17342\xc2\xb0N, 66.49231\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_24.312_N_66_29_32.316_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb224.312\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb029\xe2\x80\xb232.316\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.17342000\xc2\xb0N 66.49231000\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.17342000; -66.49231000</span></span></span></a></span></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The largest sections of the forest are located in the municipalities of Ponce and Jayuya, both of which are municipalities in the Puerto Rico Tourism Company\'s <a href="/wiki/Porta_Caribe" title="Porta Caribe">Porta Caribe</a> tourism zone.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cerro de Punta 1,338 meters (4,390&#160;ft), the highest peak in Puerto Rico, is located in the western section of the forest and the lowest elevation is found at the south edge of the forest near Salto de Inab\xc3\xb3n (Inab\xc3\xb3n Falls), an altitude of approximately 440 meters (1,440&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Forest_types">Forest types</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Forest types"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cyathea-med3.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Cyathea-med3.jpg/200px-Cyathea-med3.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Cyathea-med3.jpg/300px-Cyathea-med3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Cyathea-med3.jpg/400px-Cyathea-med3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a><figcaption>Tree ferns like this <a href="/wiki/Cyathea" title="Cyathea">Cyathea</a> are abundant at Toro Negro</figcaption></figure>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Toro_Negro_SF-3.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Toro_Negro_SF-3.png/450px-Toro_Negro_SF-3.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="398" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Toro_Negro_SF-3.png/675px-Toro_Negro_SF-3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/12/Toro_Negro_SF-3.png 2x" data-file-width="809" data-file-height="716" /></a><figcaption>Bosque Estatal Toro Negro life zone-to-elevation relationships</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Four vegetation associations have been delineated in two bioclimatic life zones.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The two climatic <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biome</a> zones are: the subtropical moist forest life zone (31% of the forest) and the lower mountain wet forest life zone (the remaining 69% of the forest). The <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a> is accentuated by a large number of steep slopes and high waterfalls.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Toro Negro subforests are catalogued on the basis of their elevation and content. From <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a>, one of the tallest peaks in the forest, four of Puerto Rico\'s distinct forest types can be seen: <a href="/wiki/Tabonuco" class="mw-redirect" title="Tabonuco">Bosque Tabonuco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buchenavia" title="Buchenavia">Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prestoea_montana" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestoea montana">Bosque Sierra de Palmas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cloud_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloud Forest">Bosque enano</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bosque_Tabonuco_forest">Bosque Tabonuco forest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bosque Tabonuco forest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>At the lower elevations of the forest (below 2,000 feet [610&#160;m] above sea level) stands the Bosque Tabonuco forest which is dominated by the majestic Tabonuco tree (<a href="/wiki/Dacryodes_excelsa" title="Dacryodes excelsa">Dacryodes excelsa</a>) that can reach up to 100 feet (30&#160;m) and grows primarily in protected sites at low elevations. The Tabonuco forest has many of the characteristics for which tropical rain forests are noted. The forest canopy has three levels: an upper level that may be as much as 35% Tabonuco, a lower canopy, and an under story. The second most prominent tree in this forest type, the <a href="/wiki/Sloanea_berteroana" title="Sloanea berteroana">Montillo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sloanea_berteroana" title="Sloanea berteroana">Sloanea berteroana</a>), has large buttress roots, typical of many rain forest trees. Such roots help support the heavy canopy of large trees growing in very wet soil. The forest floor is only scarcely vegetated, but the forest canopy is rich with aerial plants: bromeliads, orchids, vines, and arboreal ferns.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.pwnet.org_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.pwnet.org-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The tabonuco type dominates in the subtropical wet life zone.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bosque_Micropholis_Buchenavia_forest">Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia forest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia forest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Above 2,000 feet (610&#160;m) is the Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia forest. Tree height in the Micropholis Buchenavia forest is less than 50 feet (15&#160;m), and the layers of the forest canopy are less distinct than in the Tabonuco type.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.pwnet.org_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.pwnet.org-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Micropholis" title="Micropholis">Micropholis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buchenavia" title="Buchenavia">Buchenavia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Buchenavia_capitata" title="Buchenavia capitata">Granadillo</a>) are the dominant species in this lower montane zonal vegetation association.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sierra_de_Palmas_forest">Sierra de Palmas forest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sierra de Palmas forest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>At about the same elevation as the Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia forest (above 2,000 feet [610&#160;m]), but on very steep slopes, are the Sierra de Palmas forests dominated by the sierra palm (<a href="/wiki/Prestoea_montana" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestoea montana">Prestoea montana</a>). Sometimes called palm-breaker, this forest type may reach 50 feet (15&#160;m) in height.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.pwnet.org_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.pwnet.org-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Sierra de Palmas covers the largest area of all forest types in Toro Negro. The palm forest is distinguishable at a great distance by the form and size of leaves and by the general pale green color of the foliage. Below 650 meters (2,130&#160;ft) elevation the palms appear as scattered elements; however at higher elevations the sierra palm becomes a dominant species over a large area.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The trunk of the sierra palm is straight, erect, cylindrical and attains heights of 10\xe2\x80\x9315 metres (33\xe2\x80\x9349&#160;ft). The pinnate leaves are mostly 2.0\xe2\x80\x932.5 metres (6.6\xe2\x80\x938.2&#160;ft) long and cast a dense shade on the ground. The palm forest, nearly always a single species dominant is normally open and free from undergrowth of any kind. The globose fruits are somewhat more than one centimeter in diameter and produced in great abundance.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bosque_Enano_forest">Bosque Enano forest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bosque Enano forest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>At the highest elevations, near the top of <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a> and similar peaks, grows the <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">Bosque enano forest</a>, also known as dwarf forest, <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">cloud forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elfin_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Elfin forest">elfin forest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moss_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Moss forest">moss forest</a>. This forest type is composed of very dense stands of small, stunted trees and shrubs. The cloud forest has many of the same tree species as the Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia forest, but growth is limited by adverse climate\xe2\x80\x94heavy rain, strong winds, and almost constant cloud cover.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.pwnet.org_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.pwnet.org-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The dwarf or cloud forest developed in the higher peaks of the Central Cordillera is quite different in general appearance from the cloud forest of <a href="/wiki/El_Yunque_National_Forest" title="El Yunque National Forest">Sierra Luquillo Mountains</a> due to the less rigorous environment in Toro Negro. The physical effect of the wind is much reduced; the shrubs are neither bent nor shorn to an even surface, but are essentially erect and their crowns are rounded and uneven in outline. The mosses are reduced to a thin mantle on the more sheltered trunks and are absent in many places, while the great mats of <a href="/wiki/Selaginella" title="Selaginella">Selaginella</a> are completely lacking.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Toro Negro forest, only the most inaccessible mountain tops have never been cleared. Most of the lower areas are subject to the familiar routine of logging, clearing, burning, and grazing or semi-permanent cultivation. Most of the forest lands in Toro Negro rise above the upper limit of successful coffee cultivation.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geology">Geology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Toro Negro State Forest has both deep soils and surface soils. Deep soils are derived from volcanic <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">igneous rock</a>, fine-grained. These contain high amounts of permeable clay, low amounts of sand, silt, and high amounts of iron and aluminum, but little silica. The surface soils are acidic and brittle while the subsoil is acidic and heavy, but permeable. Its hills are mostly steep. Usually the <a href="/wiki/Top_soil" class="mw-redirect" title="Top soil">top soil</a> is lost by erosion.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro._13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bosque_Estatal_de_Toro_Negro.-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>There are nine rivers that flow south (<a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Inab%C3%B3n" title="R\xc3\xado Inab\xc3\xb3n">R\xc3\xado Indalecia</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guayo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guayo">R\xc3\xado Guayo</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Inab%C3%B3n" title="R\xc3\xado Inab\xc3\xb3n">R\xc3\xado Inab\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Blanco_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado Blanco (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Blanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Anon" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Anon">R\xc3\xado An\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Prieto_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Prieto (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Prieto</a>), and three that flow north (<a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Saliente" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Saliente">R\xc3\xado Saliente</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Toro_Negro" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Toro Negro">R\xc3\xado Toro Negro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Matrullas" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Matrullas">R\xc3\xado Matrullas</a>) from the forest. The Matrullas and Guineo reservoirs are also part of the forest. R\xc3\xado Toro Negro - after which the forest is named - separates the municipalities of Ciales and Orocovis; it also forms Lago El Guineo. The forest\'s other lake, Lago Matrullas, is accessible via Puerto Rico Highway 564, which can be accessed via <a href="/wiki/PR-143" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-143">PR-143</a>, in the municipality of Orocovis.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Flora">Flora</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flora"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_flora_at_Toro_Negro_State_Forest" title="List of flora at Toro Negro State Forest">List of flora at Toro Negro State Forest</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1237879389"><table class="infobox vcard"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above fn org">Fauna and Flora at Bosque Estatal de Toro Negro</th></tr><tr><td category</a> IV (habitat/species management area)</div></td></tr><tr class="locality"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> / <a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a> / <a href="/wiki/Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Orocovis, Puerto Rico">Orocovis</a> / <a href="/wiki/Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ciales, Puerto Rico">Ciales</a> / <a href="/wiki/Juana_Diaz,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Juana Diaz, Puerto Rico">Juana Diaz</a>, Puerto Rico</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Area</th><td class="infobox-data">6,945 acres (28.11&#160;km<sup>2</sup>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Elevation</th><td class="infobox-data">4,390&#160;ft (1,340&#160;m)Highest peak in Puerto Rico</td></tr><tr class="note"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Established</th><td class="infobox-data">1934<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Named for</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Toro_Negro_River" title="Toro Negro River">Toro Negro River</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Visitors</th><td class="infobox-data">126,916<sup id="cite_ref-envivopr.com_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-envivopr.com-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>(67% island residents and 33% international visitors)<sup id="cite_ref-envivopr.com_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-envivopr.com-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Governing&#160;body</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.drna.gobierno.pr/biblioteca/publicaciones/hojas-de-nuestro-ambiente/30-Toro%20Negro%20ultimo.pdf/view?searchterm=toro%20negro">Toro Negro State Forest</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Toro Negro has four vegetation associations catalogued into two subtropical moist life zones: The first is a Subtropical Moist Zone (Zona Muy H\xc3\xbameda Subtropical) and consists of the Tabonuco forest (Bosque de Tabonuco). The second is the Lower Mountain Wet Zone (Zona Muy H\xc3\xbameda Monta\xc3\xb1a Abajo). This zone consists of three sub forests: the Micropholis Buchenavia forest (Bosque Micropholis Buchenavia), the Mountain Palm forest (Bosque de Palma de Sierra), and the Dwarf forest (Bosque Enano).<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>E. L. Little and F. H. Wadsworth reported a total of 160 tree species distributed amongst 53 families.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The largest families are: <a href="/wiki/Melastomaceae" class="mw-redirect" title="Melastomaceae">Melastomaceae</a> (16 species), <a href="/wiki/Lauraceae" title="Lauraceae">Lauraceae</a> (11 species) and <a href="/wiki/Myrtaceae" title="Myrtaceae">Myrtaceae</a> (10 species).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">Ferns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid">orchids</a> are abundant. Forty of the species found in this forest are endemic to Puerto Rico and thirteen are introduced species.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The fern <a href="/wiki/Thelypteris_inabonensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Thelypteris inabonensis">Thelypteris inabonensis</a>, endemic to this forest and found only at the headwaters of Rio Inabon and at the Toro Negro\'s <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Rosa" title="Cerro Rosa">Cerro Rosa</a> in Ciales, has been identified by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service">U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service</a> as an endangered species.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the more common trees are: <i>tabonuco</i> (<a href="/wiki/Dacryodes_excelsa" title="Dacryodes excelsa">Dacryodes excelsa</a>), <i>ausubo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Manilkara_bidentata" title="Manilkara bidentata">Manilkara bidentata</a>), <i>jag\xc3\xbcilla</i> (<a href="/wiki/Magnolia_portoricensis" title="Magnolia portoricensis">Magnolia portoricensis</a>), <i>nuez moscada</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ocotea_moschata" title="Ocotea moschata">Ocotea moschata</a>), <i>granadillo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Buchenavia_capitata" title="Buchenavia capitata">Buchenavia capitata</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Montezuma_speciosissima" class="mw-redirect" title="Montezuma speciosissima">maga</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Montezuma_speciosissima" class="mw-redirect" title="Montezuma speciosissima">Montezuma speciosissima</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Vitex_divaricata" title="Vitex divaricata">hig\xc3\xbcerillo</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Vitex_divaricata" title="Vitex divaricata">Vitex divaricata</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Prunus_occidentalis" title="Prunus occidentalis">almedr\xc3\xb3n</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Prunus_occidentalis" title="Prunus occidentalis">Prunus occidentalis</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1cana" class="mw-redirect" title="J\xc3\xa1cana">j\xc3\xa1cana</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Pouteria_multiflora" title="Pouteria multiflora">Pouteria multiflora</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition <i><a href="/wiki/Prestoea_montana" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestoea montana">Palmas de sierra</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Prestoea_montana" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestoea montana">Prestoea montana</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Cyathea" title="Cyathea">helechos arb\xc3\xb3reos</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Cyathea" title="Cyathea">Cyathea</a> Sp.) are very abundant. Some of the species that were introduced to this forest are <i>mahoe</i> (<a href="/wiki/Hibiscus_elatus" title="Hibiscus elatus">Hibiscus elatus</a> Sw.), <i><a href="/wiki/Swietenia_macrophylla" title="Swietenia macrophylla">caoba hondure\xc3\xb1a</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Swietenia_macrophylla" title="Swietenia macrophylla">Swietenia macrophylla</a>), <i>pino hondure\xc3\xb1o</i> (<a href="/wiki/Pinus_caribaea" class="mw-redirect" title="Pinus caribaea">Pinus caribaea</a>), <i>eucalipto</i> (<a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus_robusta" title="Eucalyptus robusta">Eucalyptus robusta</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Neolamarckia_cadamba" title="Neolamarckia cadamba">kadam</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Neolamarckia_cadamba" title="Neolamarckia cadamba">Anthocephalus chinensis</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ilex_cookii" title="Ilex cookii">Ilex cookii</a>, commonly known as Cook\'s Holly or te, is a small evergreen <a href="/wiki/Holly" title="Holly">holly</a> shrub<sup id="cite_ref-fws.gov_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fws.gov-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> known to exist only in the Toro Negro State Forest and only in extremely limited amounts.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is listed as a <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> species by the <a href="/wiki/IUCN" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN">IUCN</a> and protected by law.<sup id="cite_ref-fws.gov_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fws.gov-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1935 and 1943,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 28 species of trees were planted in Toro Negro. Their plantings (either via seeding or via planting of saplings) consisted of both native and exotic species.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Nineteen native species were planted as follows (the quantity planted/seeded is shown after the species; and X means experimental planting only):\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Buchenavia_tetraphylla" class="mw-redirect" title="Buchenavia tetraphylla">Buchenavia tetraphylla</a>, 200</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ocotea_spathulata&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ocotea spathulata (page does not exist)">Ocotea spathulata</a>, 1,000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Calophyllum_calaba" title="Calophyllum calaba">Calophyllum calaba</a>, 52,990</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Petitia_domingensis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Petitia domingensis (page does not exist)">Petitia domingensis</a>, 9,200</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cedrela_odorata" title="Cedrela odorata">Cedrela odorata</a>, 499,526</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Podocarpus_coreacius&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Podocarpus coreacius (page does not exist)">Podocarpus coreacius</a>, X</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cordia_alliodora" title="Cordia alliodora">Cordia alliodora</a>, 553,892</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pouteria_multiflora" title="Pouteria multiflora">Pouteria multiflora</a>, 2,963,736</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dacryodes_excelsa" title="Dacryodes excelsa">Dacryodes excelsa</a>, 22,375</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prunus_occidentalis" title="Prunus occidentalis">Prunus occidentales</a>, X</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eugenia_stahlii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eugenia stahlii (page does not exist)">Eugenia stahlii</a>, 6,500</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sideroxylon_foetidissimum" title="Sideroxylon foetidissimum">Sideroxylon foetidissimum</a>, 2,098</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guarea_guidonia" title="Guarea guidonia">Guarea guidonia</a>, 109,351</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tabebuia_heterophylla" title="Tabebuia heterophylla">Tabebuia heterophylla</a>, 12,400</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hymenaea_courbaril" title="Hymenaea courbaril">Hymenaea courbaril</a>, 14</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thespesia_grandiflora" title="Thespesia grandiflora">Thespesia grandiflora</a>, 141,885</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Manilkara_bidentata" title="Manilkara bidentata">Manilkara bidentata</a>, 3,500</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vitex_divaricata" title="Vitex divaricata">Vitex divaricada</a>, 195,874</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ocotea_moschata" title="Ocotea moschata">Ocotea moschata</a>, 71,131</li></ul>\n<p>The nine exotic species were:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bambusa_vulgaris" title="Bambusa vulgaris">Bambusa vulgaris</a>, 2,350</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pinus_caribaea" class="mw-redirect" title="Pinus caribaea">Pinus caribaea</a>, X</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cupressus_lusitanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Cupressus lusitanica">Cupressus lusitanica</a>, X</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swietenia_macrophylla" title="Swietenia macrophylla">Swietenia macrophylla</a>, 764,436</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">Eucalyptus spp.</a>, 158,910</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swietenia_mahagoni" title="Swietenia mahagoni">Swietenia mahagoni</a>, 35443</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fraxinus_uhdei" title="Fraxinus uhdei">Fraxinus uhdei</a>, X</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tectona_grandis" class="mw-redirect" title="Tectona grandis">Tectona grandis</a>, 850</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hibiscus_elatus" title="Hibiscus elatus">Hibiscus elatus</a>, X</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Fauna">Fauna</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fauna"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fauna_at_Toro_Negro_State_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="List of fauna at Toro Negro State Forest">List of fauna at Toro Negro State Forest</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Guarag%C3%BCao_de_bosque,_Puerto_Rican_Broad-winged_Hawk,_Buteo_platypterus_brunnescens.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Guarag%C3%BCao_de_bosque%2C_Puerto_Rican_Broad-winged_Hawk%2C_Buteo_platypterus_brunnescens.jpg/300px-Guarag%C3%BCao_de_bosque%2C_Puerto_Rican_Broad-winged_Hawk%2C_Buteo_platypterus_brunnescens.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Guarag%C3%BCao_de_bosque%2C_Puerto_Rican_Broad-winged_Hawk%2C_Buteo_platypterus_brunnescens.jpg/450px-Guarag%C3%BCao_de_bosque%2C_Puerto_Rican_Broad-winged_Hawk%2C_Buteo_platypterus_brunnescens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Guarag%C3%BCao_de_bosque%2C_Puerto_Rican_Broad-winged_Hawk%2C_Buteo_platypterus_brunnescens.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="384" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_broad-winged_hawk" title="Puerto Rican broad-winged hawk">Puerto Rican broad-winged hawks</a> (<i>Buteo platypterus brunnescens</i>) like this one are part of Toro Negro\'s fauna</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There are 30 species of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> reported, including 6 endemic species and two that are endangered: the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_sharp-shinned_hawk" title="Puerto Rican sharp-shinned hawk">Puerto Rican sharp-shinned hawk</a> (Vernacular Spanish: <i>Falc\xc3\xb3n de sierra</i>; Taxonomy: <i>Accipiter striatus venator</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_broad-winged_hawk" title="Puerto Rican broad-winged hawk">Puerto Rican broad-winged hawk</a> (Vernacular Spanish: <i>Guarag\xc3\xbcao de bosque</i>; Taxonomy: <i>Buteo platypterus brunnescens</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_parrot" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican parrot">Puerto Rican parrot</a> (Vernacular Spanish: <i>Cotorra puertorrique\xc3\xb1a</i>; Taxonomy: <i>Amazona vittata</i>), a critically endangered species, has also been seen in this forest.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Recent studies have identified eight species of <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bats</a>. They are most visible at dusk as this is when these nocturnal critters are out foraging for food, primarily mosquitoes. The 13 species of bats living in the forest play an important ecological role in controlling mosquitoes, which not only carry diseases but also harass hikers. The three most prevalent bat species are the <a href="/wiki/Greater_bulldog_bat" title="Greater bulldog bat">greater bulldog bat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antillean_ghost-faced_bat" title="Antillean ghost-faced bat">Antillean ghost-faced bat</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sooty_mustached_bat" title="Sooty mustached bat">sooty mustached bat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-animals.pawnation.com_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-animals.pawnation.com-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>There are 20 species of <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> and, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Bufo_marinus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bufo marinus">Bufo marinus</a> (Spanish: <i>Sapo com\xc3\xban</i>), all are endemic. Reptiles include the <i><a href="/wiki/Anolis_cuvieri" title="Anolis cuvieri">Lagarto verde</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Lagarto_verde_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lagarto_verde-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (<i><a href="/wiki/Anolis_cuvieri" title="Anolis cuvieri">Anolis cuvieri</a></i>), <i><a href="/wiki/Anolis_occultus" title="Anolis occultus">lagartijo pigmeo</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Anolis_occultus" title="Anolis occultus">Anolis occultus</a></i>), and <i>boa de Puerto Rico</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Chilabothrus_inornatus" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilabothrus inornatus">Chilabothrus inornatus</a></i>), which is in danger of extinction; amphibians include the <i>siguana</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Ameiva_exsul" class="mw-redirect" title="Ameiva exsul">Ameiva exsul</a></i>) and the <i>culebra ciega</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Amphisbaena_caeca" title="Amphisbaena caeca">Amphisbaena caeca</a></i>). Amphibians include <i>coqu\xc3\xad com\xc3\xban</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Eleutherodactylus_coqui" class="mw-redirect" title="Eleutherodactylus coqui">Eleutherodactylus coqui</a></i>) and the <i>coqu\xc3\xad de la monta\xc3\xb1a</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Eleutherodactylus_portoricensis" title="Eleutherodactylus portoricensis">Eleutherodactylus portoricensis</a></i>), a species denominated as vulnerable under Puerto Rico Law 6766.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Small_Asian_mongoose" title="Small Asian mongoose">Small Asian mongoose</a> (Vernacular Spanish: <i>Mangosta peque\xc3\xb1a asi\xc3\xa1tica</i>; Taxonomy: <i>Herpestes javanicus</i>), has also been spotted inhabiting this forest.<sup id="cite_ref-animals.pawnation.com_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-animals.pawnation.com-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Toro Negro State Forest is home to 11 species of snakes, all non-venomous to humans. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_boa" title="Puerto Rican boa">Puerto Rican boa</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Chilabothrus_inornatus" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilabothrus inornatus">Chilabothrus inornatus</a></i>) grows to 6\xe2\x80\x937 feet (1.8\xe2\x80\x932.1&#160;m) in length and weighs about 2 pounds (0.91&#160;kg). It is a heavy-bodied snake with tan to dark brown body color and dark blotches down its back. It will defend itself with a bite, but kills its prey by suffocation. It is a protected species due to over-harvesting to collect oil and skins. It is nocturnal and prefers to remain under cover during the day and hunt at night. The <a href="/wiki/Borikenophis_portoricensis" title="Borikenophis portoricensis">Puerto Rican racer</a> (<i>Culebra Corredora</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alsophis_portoricensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Alsophis portoricensis">Alsophis portoricensis</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) grows to 3 feet (0.91&#160;m). It slinks around in the trees of the Toro Negro Forest. His body sports a solid brown color with each of his scales edged by a darker brown. Like the forest\'s other various garden snakes, it is a daytime hunter. The forest also features <a href="/wiki/Blind_snake" class="mw-redirect" title="Blind snake">blind snakes</a>. They spend nearly their entire lives underground but do sometimes take cover under rotting trees. They do not bite as they do not have teeth.<sup id="cite_ref-animals.pawnation.com_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-animals.pawnation.com-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Olivo_(aka,_Ceti)_(English%3DSirajo_Goby)_(Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Olivo_%28aka%2C_Ceti%29_%28English%3DSirajo_Goby%29_%28Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri%29.jpg/220px-Olivo_%28aka%2C_Ceti%29_%28English%3DSirajo_Goby%29_%28Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="103" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Olivo_%28aka%2C_Ceti%29_%28English%3DSirajo_Goby%29_%28Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri%29.jpg/330px-Olivo_%28aka%2C_Ceti%29_%28English%3DSirajo_Goby%29_%28Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Olivo_%28aka%2C_Ceti%29_%28English%3DSirajo_Goby%29_%28Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri%29.jpg/440px-Olivo_%28aka%2C_Ceti%29_%28English%3DSirajo_Goby%29_%28Taxonomy%3DSicydium_plumieri%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="211" /></a><figcaption>The Olivo fish (<i><a href="/wiki/Sicydium_plumieri" title="Sicydium plumieri">Sicydium plumieri</a></i>), common in waters of the forest</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Its rivers and lakes are home to several species of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crustacean" title="Crustacean">crustaceans</a>.  Fish found here include <i><a href="/wiki/Agonostomus_monticola" class="mw-redirect" title="Agonostomus monticola">Dajao</a></i> (Vernacular English: <i><a href="/wiki/Mountain_Mullet" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain Mullet">Mountain Mullet</a></i>; Taxonomy: <i><a href="/wiki/Agonostomus_monticola" class="mw-redirect" title="Agonostomus monticola">Agonostomus monticola</a></i>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Sicydium_plumieri" title="Sicydium plumieri">Olivo</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sicydium_plumieri" title="Sicydium plumieri">Sicydium plumieri</a></i>), also known as <i><a href="/wiki/Sicydium_plumieri" title="Sicydium plumieri">Ceti</a></i>. Some crustaceans are the <i><a href="/wiki/Camar%C3%B3n_bocu" class="mw-redirect" title="Camar\xc3\xb3n bocu">camar\xc3\xb3n bocu</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Macrobrachium_crenulatum" title="Macrobrachium crenulatum">Macrobrachium crenulatum</a></i>), <i><a href="/wiki/Atya_lanipes" title="Atya lanipes">gata</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Atya_lanipes" title="Atya lanipes">Atya lanipes</a></i>), and <i><a href="/wiki/Buruquena" class="mw-redirect" title="Buruquena">buruquena</a></i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Epilobocera_sinuatifrons" title="Epilobocera sinuatifrons">Epilobocera sinuatifrons</a></i>), all endemic to Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Facilities">Facilities</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Facilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>With the exception of the <i>Salto de Do\xc3\xb1a Juana</i> waterfall, all of the forest facilities, including all trails, are located within the municipality of Orocovis<sup id="cite_ref-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis._56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis.-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and they are collectively known as the <i>Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Recreational Area</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Guided tours are available or visitors explore on their own. <a href="/wiki/Zipline" class="mw-redirect" title="Zipline">Ziplining</a> is also a common activity in the Toro Negro forest.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The forest office, staffed by personnel from the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a>, provides maps of the forest and its trails and services, weather conditions information, and mud slides danger levels.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_State_Forest._11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_State_Forest.-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among the facilities available at Toro Negro are a camping area, a recreational area, a system of hiking trails and observation points.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Trails">Trails</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Trails"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Officially there are 10 hiking trails covering 18 kilometers (11&#160;mi). They are provided for hiking as well as to facilitate bird and landscape watching, meditation, and similar activities.  While the official number of trails is stated as 10, some of the trails are actually dirt roads for <a href="/wiki/Park_ranger" title="Park ranger">park ranger</a> vehicles. Also, some of the "trails" require the hiker to walk a segment on a paved Commonwealth road or county road. Trails are generally quite wide, but being a forest in mountains with high humidity and rain precipitation, many of the trails are muddy in at least some areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Hikers are often seen with <a href="/wiki/Walking_stick" title="Walking stick">walking sticks</a>, which help maintain balance when walking on slippery surfaces, particularly the algae-covered ground rocks present on some of the trails.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some of the trails lead to or run near <i>charcos</i>. Charcos are natural swimming pools (swimming holes).<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The Toro Negro State Forest office is the starting point for several of the trails. However, most of the trails are not well marked, nor are they well kept, so they can be hard to locate and to follow in the dense forest.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_State_Forest._11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_State_Forest.-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Under an agreement with the government of Puerto Rico, the municipality of Orocovis is the entity responsible for trail maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The 10 official trails are:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>No.</th>\n<th>Trail Name</th>\n<th>Features</th>\n<th>Description</th>\n<th>Approx<br />length<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NEGRO_2013_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEGRO_2013-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></th>\n<th>Notes</th>\n<th>Northern Terminus</th>\n<th>Southern Terminus\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>Camino El Bolo</td>\n<td align="left"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinnbild_Wanderer_bgw.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Hiking" miles (4.8&#160;km)</td>\n<td align="left">Connects to trails # 3 and #6</td>\n<td>PR-143, Northeast of the Visitors Center</td>\n<td>Visitors Center, PR-143, Km
