/></a></span>&#160; \xe2\x80\x93 Indicates Visitors\' Center\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#1_(&quot;El_Bolo&quot;)"><span id="Trail_.231_.28.22El_Bolo.22.29"></span>Trail #1 ("<i>El Bolo</i>")</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Trail #1 (&quot;El Bolo&quot;)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Named <i>Camino El Bolo</i>, it is the forest\'s longest trail, about 2 miles (3.2&#160;km) long, and essentially a loop around <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Bolo" title="Cerro El Bolo">Cerro El Bolo</a>. This trail has its course along <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Bolo" title="Cerro El Bolo">Cerro El Bolo</a> (El Bolo Mountain), Puerto Rico\'s tenth tallest peak at 3,527 feet (1,075&#160;m) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-geonames.usgs.gov_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geonames.usgs.gov-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is a low challenge trail. It is essentially a loop that starts at the visitors\' parking area on PR-143 and terminates on PR-143 about 1/4 mile north of the visitors\' parking area, from where hikers simply walk the road back to the parking area. Starting off at the visitors\' parking area, hikers cross PR-143 to head south on the trail. This section of the forest has many <a href="/wiki/Banana_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Banana tree">banana trees</a> and flowers along its way and starts off with a steep uphill climb. Approximately 0.4 miles (0.64&#160;km) into the trail, the trail starts to head East and flattens out as it becomes a rocky at first and then grassy further on. Another 0.4 miles (0.64&#160;km) heading East the trail connects to Trail #6 which leads to the swimming pool. Continuing East another 0.2 miles (0.32&#160;km), the trail becomes uphill again as it connects to the northernmost point of a paved road, Puerto Rico Highway 561, on the right hand side. From this point on the trail starts to head North on a downhill grade but in less than 0.1 miles (0.16&#160;km) it connects to Trail #3 which leads to the Observation Tower, where there is a sign that reads <i>La Torre</i> ("The Tower"). The trail continuous downhill North-Northwest about 0.8 miles (1.3&#160;km) until it reaches paved road PR-143, in the vicinity of km 32.6. From this point hikers make a left to walk southwest bound on PR-143 (that is, "West" on PR-143) until reaching the visitors\' area at km 32.4.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#3_(Observation_Tower)"><span id="Trail_.233_.28Observation_Tower.29"></span>Trail #3 (Observation Tower)</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Trail #3 (Observation Tower)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This trail leads to the Observation Tower. This trail if for advanced hikers. Trail #3 does not start at the visitors\' parking area, so hikers must first hike on other trails to get to Trail #3.  Starting from the visitors\' parking area, there are three ways to get to Trail #3. Path Option 1: This is the shortest route. Hikers get on PR-143, walking northeast bound (that is, making a left from the parking area to head "East" on PR-143) about 0.25 miles, make a right into the forest at the sign ("<i>Verada #6 - Piscina</i>") to get on Trail #6, hike the 0.8 mile of Trail #6 to its end, make a left into Trail #1 and hike about 0.3 mile to the beginning of Trail #3. Path Option 2: This is the second shortest route. Hikers take Trail #1 as described above under section "Trail #1" until they reach Trail #3 where there is a sign that reads "Observation Tower".  Path Option 3: This is the longest route. Hikers head northeast bound (that is, "East" on PR-143) passed the sign stating "Trail #6 - La Piscina (this will be about 0.25 mile hike), and continue northeast bound for approximately another 0.25 mile until the sign stating "Trail #1 - Camino Bolo where hikers make a right into the forest and continue this trail about 0.9 mile until coming to Trail #3.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Once on Trail #3, hikers climb this trail about 0.6 miles to its top where the observation tower is located.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The trail to the observation tower <a href="/wiki/Lookout" title="Lookout">lookout</a> hill is not for the faint of heart. It is very steep and very slippery. It is a one-way trail (in the sense that the same trail is used in the return trip) and the trail feels even more slippery in the downhill return hike. This trail is made of rocks but, because of the high humidity and low traffic, <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> have overtaken the rocks to make the trail very slippery. Walking around the rocks does not always help as the area is <a href="/wiki/Mud" title="Mud">muddy</a> - though albeit less slippery. The view and fresh air and breeze make the trek quite rewarding. The views are unobstructed and panoramic 360\xc2\xb0 views are possible. The tower is 3,537 feet above sea level. Altogether the distance from the visitors\' parking area to the tower is 2.14 miles.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#5_(&quot;Las_Cuarenta&quot;)"><span id="Trail_.235_.28.22Las_Cuarenta.22.29"></span>Trail #5 ("<i>Las Cuarenta</i>")</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Trail #5 (&quot;Las Cuarenta&quot;)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Trail #5 is about 0.9 mile long and is a medium challenge trail. There is a significant amount of mud on this trail, but less so in the dry season months of December through March and June through July. To reach this trail from the visitors\' parking area hikers must first head northbound to trek the entire length of Trail #7 (the Camping Area trail, 0.1 mile long), cross the bridge over the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Creek and then hop on Trail #8. From this point on Trail #8, hikers head West for about 0.2 mile where Trail #5 begins; its entrance is located on the right hand side. The trail heads North and leads to Puerto Rico Highway 564. The first segment of the trail runs downhill for 0.9 mile.  The trail runs a thick tropical jungle of banana trees, sierra palms, tree ferns, <a href="/wiki/Flamboyant_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Flamboyant tree">flamboyant trees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Araceae" title="Araceae">elephant ears</a>. The trail is muddy, steep, and scantily-marked. Visibility is minimal through the dense foliage.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are several creeks near this trail and birds are abundant: <a href="/wiki/Black-throated_blue_warbler" title="Black-throated blue warbler">black-throated blue warblers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_parula" title="Northern parula">northern parulas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_mango" title="Green mango">green mangos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_May_warbler" title="Cape May warbler">Cape May warblers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belted_kingfisher" title="Belted kingfisher">belted kingfishers</a>, among others. After the 0.9 mile trek, the trail reaches PR-564. There is <a href="/wiki/Water_pump" class="mw-redirect" title="Water pump">water pumping station</a> on the left. From this point the "trail" turns right, as PR-564 is intended to be part of the trail. Hikers walk South on PR-564 for 0.6 mile where the northern terminus of Trail #9 (the Do\xc3\xb1a Petra trail) is located to the right. Continuing southbound on PR-564 for another 0.1 mile, the road trail meets PR-143, where hikers turn right to continue South on Trail #5. From this point hikers walk another 0.25 mile to arrive at the visitors\' parking area on the right side of the road. Considering the hikes on Trails #7 and #8 plus the hikes on roads PR-564 and PR-143, Trail #5 is 2.95 miles long, making it the second longest hike of all of Toro Negro\'s trails.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#6_(The_Pool)"><span id="Trail_.236_.28The_Pool.29"></span>Trail #6 (The Pool)</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Trail #6 (The Pool)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This trail is about 0.5 miles long and a low challenge trail. The trail is well maintained, but the natural pool that it leads to is open during summer months only. Starting from the visitors\' parking area, hikers get on PR-143 walking northeast bound (that is, making a left from the parking area to head "East" on PR-143) about 0.25 miles, then make a right into the forest at the sign ("<i>Verada #6 - Piscina</i>") to get on Trail #6. This trail runs along a river for about 1/4 mile before it comes to the sign "Piscina" pointing left. Continuing south on the trail, there are two eye-catching <a href="/wiki/Waterfall" title="Waterfall">waterfalls</a> visible from the trail. Continuing southbound and uphill, the trail goes through two flat and open areas with <a href="/wiki/Picnic" title="Picnic">picnic</a> tables. After this, the trail continues uphill and southbound for about 0.6 miles where it comes to its end, reaching Trail #1. Once at Trail #1, hikers either make a left or a right to get onto Trail #1 (trail #1 is a loop trail) or, of course, may turn around to return to the parking area via Trail #6. The entire length of Trail #6 is 0.8 miles.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#7_(Camping_Area)"><span id="Trail_.237_.28Camping_Area.29"></span>Trail #7 (Camping Area)</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Trail #7 (Camping Area)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This trail is actually a paved forest road leading to the <i>Los Viveros</i> camping area, Toro Negro State Forest\'s only <a href="/wiki/Campground" class="mw-redirect" title="Campground">campground</a>. It is located north of the parking area.  The "trail" is only 0.1 mile long, wide and flat, thus a low challenge trail. The trail is also the connecting trail to Trail #8, which leads to <i>Charco La Confesora</i> (see below). Another use of this trail is that it leads to one of the forest\'s three official picnic areas. Its picnic area is the one closes to the visitors\' parking area. The Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Creek runs next to the picnic area.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#8_(&quot;Charco_La_Confesora&quot;)"><span id="Trail_.238_.28.22Charco_La_Confesora.22.29"></span>Trail #8 ("<i>Charco La Confesora</i>")</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Trail #8 (&quot;Charco La Confesora&quot;)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This trail is 0.54 mile long, it is a medium challenge trail, and leads to <i>El Charco</i> ("The Pond"), a natural swimming hole. It is located north of the parking area, and starts at the end of Trail #7. After hiking north from the parking area on Trail #7 (Trail #7 is a 0.1 mile long paved road), and hiking by the <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">camping</a> area, Trail #7 comes to an end at the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana <a href="/wiki/Stream" title="Stream">Creek</a>. There is a sign pointing West (<i>Charco Confesora</i>) near the picnic area next to the camping area that serves as a landmark. At this point hikers walk over a little bridge to cross the creek, where Trail #8 begins. The trail heads northwest along the creek (the creek is located to the left of the trail) and the trail is abundant with wild flowers. It is a downhill trail and a bit muddy. A section of the trail consists of concrete steps. At the end of the trail is Charco La Confesora, a natural "pool", with a waterfall as a backdrop. swimming is allowed at this <i>charco</i>. The return path is the same as the path to the <i>charco</i> as the trail terminates at the <i>charco</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#9_(&quot;Do\xc3\xb1a_Petra&quot;)"><span id="Trail_.239_.28.22Do.C3.B1a_Petra.22.29"></span>Trail #9 ("<i>Do\xc3\xb1a Petra</i>")</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Trail #9 (&quot;Do\xc3\xb1a Petra&quot;)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This trail is 0.4 mile long, it is a medium challenge trail. Like Trail #5, it is located north of the parking area, and starts where Trail #7 end. Also, like trail #5, there is a significant amount of mud on this trail, though less so during the dry season months of December through March and June through July. To reach this trail from the visitors\' parking area hikers must first head northbound to trek the entire length of Trail #7 (the Camping Area trail, 0.1 mile long) and cross the bridge over the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Creek. Trail #9 begins at this bridge. Heading to the left from the bridge is the path for Trail #8, but heading straight up (northbound) gets hikers onto Trail #9, the Do\xc3\xb1a Petra Trail. (Like trail #5, the "<i>Las Cuarenta</i>" trail, Trail #9 will also bring the hiker to State Route PR-564, but being a shorter trail, it does not encounter PR-564 as far north as Trail #5 does.) The first segment of the trail runs downhill for 0.2 mile, where according to ranger office maps, there used to be a trail to the left (i.e., westbound) leading to Trail #5. However, vegetation apparently overran such connecting trail because it is no longer visible. The trail then continues another 0.2 mile where it reaches PR-564. From this point the "trail" turns right, as PR-564 is intended to be part of the trail. Hikers walk South on PR-564 for 0.1 mile where the "road trail" meets PR-143. At State Route PR-143 hikers turn right to continue South on Trail #9. From this point hikers walk another 0.25 mile to arrive at the visitors\' parking area on the right side of the road. Considering the hikes on Trail #7 and roads PR-564 and PR-143, Trail #9 is 0.75 mile long.<sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trails_#2,_#4,_and_#10"><span id="Trails_.232.2C_.234.2C_and_.2310"></span>Trails #2, #4, and #10</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Trails #2, #4, and #10"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Trails #2, #4 and #10 are no longer active trails. Trail #2 was called <i>Camino Ortolaza</i> and was 0.5 mile long. It was a "one-way" trail (i.e., same entrance and exit) and ran from PR-143 to the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Creek. It started on PR-143 some 0.25 mile west of the entrance to the Area Recreativa/visitors\' parking area and headed North ending at the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Creek, about 0.2 mile west of <i>Charco La Confesora</i>. Trail #4 was called <i>Camino Vega Grande</i> and was 0.4 mile long. It was another "one-way" trail and began on PR-143 about 0.1 mile east of the current Trail #1 eastern terminus. Trail #10 was called <i>Camino El Tabonuco</i> and was about 0.2 mile long. It was also a "one-way" trail. It originated at km 32.3 on PR-143 and headed north into the forest.<sup id="cite_ref-NEGRO_2013_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEGRO_2013-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-puertoricodaytrips.com_66-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertoricodaytrips.com-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Trail_#11_(T9-to-T5_Connector)"><span id="Trail_.2311_.28T9-to-T5_Connector.29"></span>Trail #11 (T9-to-T5 Connector)</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Trail #11 (T9-to-T5 Connector)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>An unnamed trail, but referenced and marked in the DRNA maps, is a trail that could be termed Trail #11 for referential purposes. It was located midway on Trail #9 (that is, about 0.2 mile west of PR-546) and headed north to Trail #5. It met Trail #9 at a point about 0.2 mile west of PR-546. This trail was about 0.3 mile long. It served the double purpose of acting as a nature trail while at the same time it connected Trails 5 and 9, thus making for a shortcut from Trail #5 back to the car parking area via Trail #9. DRNA considers this unnamed trail a part of (an offshoot of) Trail #5.<sup id="cite_ref-NEGRO_2013_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEGRO_2013-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Campgrounds">Campgrounds</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Campgrounds"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1237879389"><hr /><hr /><hr /><hr /><table class="infobox vcard" route</span></a></th><td class="infobox-data">End of PR-539 South, then Hike</td></tr>\n\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1237879389"><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader nickname"><a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a> \xe2\x80\x93 4th highest at <i>Toro Negro</i></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #E7DCC3;">Highest&#160;point</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Summit" title="Summit">Elevation</a></th><td class="infobox-data">1,205&#160;m (3,953&#160;ft)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Topographic_prominence" title="Topographic prominence">Prominence</a></th><td class="infobox-data">5th highest peak in Puerto Rico<br />Site of <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla_murders" title="Cerro Maravilla murders">Cerro Maravilla murders</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_9_11_N_66_33_15_W_type:mountain"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb09\xe2\x80\xb211\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb033\xe2\x80\xb215\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.15306\xc2\xb0N 66.55417\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.15306; -66.55417</span></span></span></a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" (3,471&#160;ft)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Topographic_prominence" title="Topographic prominence">Prominence</a></th><td class="infobox-data">12th highest peak in Puerto Rico</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_9_11_N_66_33_15_W_type:mountain"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb09\xe2\x80\xb211\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb033\xe2\x80\xb215\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.15306\xc2\xb0N 66.55417\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.15306; -66.55417</span></span></span></a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #E7DCC3;">Geography</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data label"><a href="/wiki/Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico" title="Orocovis, Puerto Rico">Orocovis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range"><span class="nowrap">Parent range</span></a></th><td class="infobox-data category"><a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Central, Puerto Rico">Cordillera Central</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #E7DCC3;">Climbing</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Normal_route" title="Normal route"><span class="nowrap">Easiest route</span></a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/PR-143" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-143">PR-143</a>, km 32.4</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Campground" class="mw-redirect" title="Campground">campgrounds</a> (camping area) at Toro Negro is called <i>Los Viveros</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis._56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis.-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  It is located on PR-143, Km 32.5.<sup id="cite_ref-XI9rCbRKR4C_2013_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XI9rCbRKR4C_2013-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  Its coordinates are at 18.17502\xc2\xb0N, 66.49202\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_30.0714_N_66_29_31.2714_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb230.0714\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb029\xe2\x80\xb231.2714\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.175019833\xc2\xb0N 66.492019833\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.175019833; -66.492019833</span></span></span></a></span></span>). Camping is available for a maximum of 35 people.<sup id="cite_ref-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis._56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis.-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Camping facilities include restrooms and showers.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A permit is required for camping and they are purchased in advance, as there are no permit sales on premises.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In the proximity of the campgrounds there is also a picnic area. It has six picnic shelters with covered <a href="/wiki/BBQ" class="mw-redirect" title="BBQ">BBQ</a>, on-site water, and a spot for a campfire.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Lakes_and_water_sports">Lakes and water sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Lakes and water sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Lake El Guineo and Lake Matrullas are both man-made reservoirs. Fishing, boating and <a href="/wiki/Kayak" title="Kayak">kayaking</a> is allowed at the El Guineo and Matrullas reservoirs.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Lake El Guineo is located at 18.1579\xc2\xb0N 66.5284\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_9_28.44_N_66_31_42.24_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb09\xe2\x80\xb228.44\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb031\xe2\x80\xb242.24\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.1579000\xc2\xb0N 66.5284000\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.1579000; -66.5284000</span></span></span></a></span></span>), at an altitude of 3,002 feet above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-trails.com_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trails.com-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is located between the municipalities of Ciales and Orocovis, west of the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Recreation Area, on PR-143 at km 25.4.<sup id="cite_ref-trails.com_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trails.com-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The lowest temperatures recorded on the Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x94some 40&#160;\xc2\xb0F (4&#160;\xc2\xb0C) -- were measured at Lake Guineo.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Lake Matrullas is located at 18.2064\xc2\xb0N 66.4798\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_12_23.0394_N_66_28_47.2794_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb012\xe2\x80\xb223.0394\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb028\xe2\x80\xb247.2794\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.206399833\xc2\xb0N 66.479799833\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.206399833; -66.479799833</span></span></span></a></span></span>), at an altitude of 2,464 feet above sea level.  It too is between the municipalities of Ciales and Orocovis. It is located northeast of the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Recreation Area, on PR-564 at km 6.1.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Puerto Rico DRNA allows the use of <a href="/wiki/Kayak" title="Kayak">kayaks</a> in Lake Matrullas. The ambiance is cool and misty. Both lakes are all well stocked with <a href="/wiki/Peacock_bass" title="Peacock bass">Peacock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Largemouth_bass" title="Largemouth bass">Largemouth bass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Creeks are abundant in the area, and in addition to the Quebrada Do\xc3\xb1a Juana, the forest also has a number of other creeks, such as Quebrada Rosa.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Observation_tower">Observation tower</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Observation tower"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The observation tower, accessible only on foot via Trail #3, rises at 3,537 feet above sea level, making it the highest manmade point on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The observation tower sits atop <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Do%C3%B1a_Juana" title="Cerro Do\xc3\xb1a Juana">Cerro Do\xc3\xb1a Juana</a>, Puerto Rico\'s 11th highest peak at 3,474 feet (1,059&#160;m) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-geonames.usgs.gov_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geonames.usgs.gov-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The tower\'s coordinates are 18.17178\xc2\xb0N, 66.48091\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_18.4074_N_66_28_51.2754_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb218.4074\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb028\xe2\x80\xb251.2754\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.171779833\xc2\xb0N 66.480909833\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.171779833; -66.480909833</span></span></span></a></span></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The tower is used for observation of the landscape surrounding Toro Negro and, on clear mornings before the afternoon clouds roll in, both the northern and southern shores of Puerto Rico are visible. <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> is also visible as a distant haze in the northeastern horizon.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The observation tower affords views Lake El Guineo and Lake Guayabal as well as the Caribbean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was built by the <a href="/wiki/Spaniard" class="mw-redirect" title="Spaniard">Spaniards</a> during colonial times as a lookout tower to protect the south coast of the Island.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (October 2015)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Charcos"><i>Charcos</i></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Charcos"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Charcos are natural ponds, or swimming holes, formed by the mountain rivers as they fall as waterfalls onto the ground below. They are popular way of refreshing from the summer heat in the Toro Negro State Forest. The forest\'s "official" pool is accessed via Trail number 6, the <i>La Piscina</i> ("The Pool") trail. To reach trail 6, hikers start out from the forest office/parking area and hike north on route PR-143 about 1/4 mile. Trail 6 is located on the right hand side of the road. This pool is a river-fed pool. It became deteriorated, in disrepair and closed to public use sometime prior to 2010 and, in February 2013, there were unconfirmed reports that it had been repaired and reopen. In 2008, it was reported that an agreement between DNRA and the local community had been signed whereby the community would help repair the pool.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Under an agreement with the government of Puerto Rico, the municipality of Orocovis is the entity responsible for pool maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In any case, this pool opens only during the summer months. The pool\'s water temperature is very chilled, but refreshing, given the high humidity of the area, particularly in the afternoons.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest._60-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiking_in_Toro_Negro_Forest.-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> La Piscina is located at 18.1713\xc2\xb0N 66.4876\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_16.52_N_66_29_15.53_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb216.52\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb029\xe2\x80\xb215.53\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.1712556\xc2\xb0N 66.4876472\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.1712556; -66.4876472</span></span></span></a></span></span>).\n</p><p>A second river-fed swimming pool <i>charco</i> is located at <i>Charco La Confesora</i>. It is about 15 x 25 feet large and deep enough to dive feet first.<sup id="cite_ref-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis._56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bosque_Toro_Negro,_Orocovis.-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  This <i>charco</i> is accessed via Trail number 8, located at the end of Trail 7, the trail to the camping area.<sup id="cite_ref-XI9rCbRKR4C_2013_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XI9rCbRKR4C_2013-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The pool at <i>Charco La Confesora</i> is located at 18.176901, -66.495861. (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_36.8436_N_66_29_45.0996_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb236.8436\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb029\xe2\x80\xb245.0996\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.176901000\xc2\xb0N 66.495861000\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.176901000; -66.495861000</span></span></span></a></span></span>).\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cerro_de_Punta_and_other_peaks">Cerro de Punta and other peaks</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cerro de Punta and other peaks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG/220px-Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG/330px-Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG/440px-Cerro_Punta_Puerto_Rico.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a>, Puerto Rico\'s tallest peak, located in the western segment of Toro Negro (photo taken from <a href="/wiki/PR-149" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-149">PR-149</a>, near the mountain top)</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monte_Jayuya" title="Monte Jayuya">Monte Jayuya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Rosa" title="Cerro Rosa">Cerro Rosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Bolo" title="Cerro El Bolo">Cerro El Bolo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Do%C3%B1a_Juana" title="Cerro Do\xc3\xb1a Juana">Cerro Do\xc3\xb1a Juana</a></div>\n<p>The forest includes Puerto Rico\'s highest peak, <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a>, which is located at km. 17.0 on Puerto Rico Highway 143.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is at 18.1722\xc2\xb0N, 66.5917\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_19.8_N_66_35_30.03_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb219.8\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb035\xe2\x80\xb230.03\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.172167\xc2\xb0N 66.5916750\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.172167; -66.5916750</span></span></span></a></span></span>). The mountain is the dividing landmark for the municipalities of Ponce and Jayuya. The mountain is accessible by car but the road is quite steep and many prefer to walk the road (it is about half hour\'s hike to the top) unless riding on an <a href="/wiki/All-wheel_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="All-wheel drive">all-wheel drive</a> vehicle.  There is parking on PR-143 for those who prefer to walk to the hilltop.  Another peak in the Toro Negro is <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a>, infamous due to the murders of two <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_independence_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico independence movement">independentistas</a> youth at the hand of police in an ambush. This peak is also accessible by car from PR-143. The road leading to the top of Cerro Maravilla is <a href="/wiki/PR-577" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-577">PR-577</a> and is not as steep as that to Cerro de Punta (the Cerro de Punta road has no state signing.) This road is also much shorter, about 0.5 kilometer total length. Cerro Maravilla is located at 18.1532\xc2\xb0N, 66.5543\xc2\xb0W (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_9_11.6_N_66_33_15.56_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb09\xe2\x80\xb211.6\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb033\xe2\x80\xb215.56\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.153222\xc2\xb0N 66.5543222\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.153222; -66.5543222</span></span></span></a></span></span>).  Communications towers for radio, television, cellular and similar systems are located atop each of these peaks and armed security personnel, including police, is on the premises. However, private individuals can access both of these peaks.  Overall, the Forest contains Cerro Punta,<sup id="cite_ref-arkive.org_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arkive.org-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Rosa" title="Cerro Rosa">Cerro Rosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Jayuya" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerro Jayuya">Cerro Jayuya</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-arkive.org_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arkive.org-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which are considered to be Puerto Rico\'s three highest peaks.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerro_El_Bolo" title="Cerro El Bolo">Cerro El Bolo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Do%C3%B1a_Juana" title="Cerro Do\xc3\xb1a Juana">Cerro Do\xc3\xb1a Juana</a> are also located within the Toro Negro Forest.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Nearby_attractions">Nearby attractions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Nearby attractions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Do\xc3\xb1a_Juana_Falls"><span id="Do.C3.B1a_Juana_Falls"></span>Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Falls</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Falls"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana,_Orocovis,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana%2C_Orocovis%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana%2C_Orocovis%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana%2C_Orocovis%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana%2C_Orocovis%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana%2C_Orocovis%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Salto_Do%C3%B1a_Juana%2C_Orocovis%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>Salto Do\xc3\xb1a Juana (Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Falls)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>These falls (Spanish: Salto de Do\xc3\xb1a Juana) are about 200 feet tall. They are not located within the Toro Negro State Forest itself but they are near it, requiring visitors to drive 3.9&#160;km westbound on route PR-143 from the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Recreational Area to reach PR-149, then drive an additional 2.3 kilometers northbound on PR-149 (towards Ciales). The falls are on PR-149 at km 41.3.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_State_Forest._11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_State_Forest.-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-XI9rCbRKR4C_2013_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XI9rCbRKR4C_2013-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They are the tallest waterfalls in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Their coordinates are 18.182836, -66.512257. (<span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;params=18_10_58.2096_N_66_30_44.1252_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">18\xc2\xb010\xe2\x80\xb258.2096\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">66\xc2\xb030\xe2\x80\xb244.1252\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">18.182836000\xc2\xb0N 66.512257000\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">18.182836000; -66.512257000</span></span></span></a></span></span>).\n</p><p>The falls are part of the Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Creek as it runs into Rio Toro Negro at the line that divides the municipalities of Ciales and Orocovis. The falls are very accessible, as they are viewable from the road as drivers cross the bridge of these falls. The falls fall next to the road on its eastern side and then run under the PR-149 bridge, to feed into Rio Toro Negro located a few yards on the western side of PR-149.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Villalba-Orocovis_Lookout">Villalba-Orocovis Lookout</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Villalba-Orocovis Lookout"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>This lookout position (known in Spanish as the <i>Mirador Villalba-Orocovis</i> or the Villalba-Orocovis Lookout) is located outside the Toro Negro State Forest but still on PR-143 (km 39.8<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) and a short distance from the forest, and it is a popular stop over for visitors to the forest. It contains picnic areas, restroom facilities and various trails.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is located at 18\xc2\xb010\'37"N, 66\xc2\xb027\'0"W,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that is, 7.4 kilometers east of Toro Negro State Forest\'s Do\xc3\xb1a Juana Recreational Area.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Climate">Climate</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Toro Negro State Forest is located in the cool, moist mountains of the Cordillera Central. Mean annual temperature from 19.4 to 25&#160;\xc2\xb0C.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Temperatures are unmistakably cooler at higher elevations.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Average yearly temperature is 18.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (65.12&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Average annual precipitation of five weather stations in and surrounding the forest ranges from 203 to 292&#160;cm.<sup id="cite_ref-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve._22-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toro_Negro_Forest_Reserve.-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As much as 150 inches of annual rainfall has registered at Toro Negro.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The average annual rainfall is 110&#160;inches. The months of September and May experience the most precipitation. A dry season runs from December through March. The months of June and July also tend to be dry.<sup id="cite_ref-drna.gobierno.pr_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drna.gobierno.pr-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Puerto Rico DRNA erroneously calls this species <i><a href="/wiki/Manilkara_zapota" title="Manilkara zapota">Manilkara zapota</a></i>, which is a different species (of the same genus <i><a href="/wiki/Manilkara" title="Manilkara">Manilkara</a></i>) cultivated for its <i><a href="/wiki/N%C3%ADspero" title="N\xc3\xadspero">n\xc3\xadspero</a></i> fruit. The correct species for the <i>Ausubo</i> tree is <i><a href="/wiki/Manilkara_bidentata" title="Manilkara bidentata">Manilkara bidentata</a></i>, a tree cultivated for its lumber. In addition note that the (erroneous) scientific name given by the DRNA (<i><a href="/wiki/Manilkara_zapota" title="Manilkara zapota">Manilkara zapota</a></i>) is never known as <i>Ausubo</i>. Its common name would be <i><a href="/wiki/Sapodilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Sapodilla">Sapodilla</a></i>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Lagarto_verde-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Lagarto_verde_52-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Puerto Rico DRNA erroneously calls this species <i>Lagartijo gigante</i>. Its correct common name is Spanish is <i>Lagarto verde</i>. (See citations to <i><a href="/wiki/Anolis_cuvieri" title="Anolis cuvieri">Anolis cuvieri</a></i>)</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="References">References</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Negro_State_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: References"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239543626"><div class="reflist reflist-columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 30em;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Hojas_de_Nuestro_Ambiente.-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Hojas_de_Nuestro_Ambiente._1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hojas_de_Nuestro_Ambiente._1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hojas_de_Nuestro_Ambiente._1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hojas_de_Nuestro_Ambiente._1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hojas_de_Nuestro_Ambiente._1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://drna.pr.gov/p-030-de-julio-de-2008/"><i>Hojas de Nuestro Ambiente</i></a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link tagged February 2019">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup>.
